Local News

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Pays Attention to New Tax Rates 101

Investigating Regulations Set by Various Provinces

Requesting a Percentage for Protecting the Cigarette Industry

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce is paying close attention to the unified tax, consumption tax, and various tax rates and collection methods newly implemented after the abolition of the Likin tax. What follows is a record of the news regarding the new taxes handled by the Chamber yesterday:

Collecting Regulations Set by Various Provinces: Yesterday, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent telegrams to the Finance Departments of various provinces, the Finance Commissioners' Offices, and the Provincial Chambers of Commerce Joint Associations, stating: "Since being granted permission to abolish the Likin and reform the special consumption tax and business tax to compensate for the accumulated ills of the past decades, we are deeply gratified that such a move has been made. However, the reform of new taxes is closely related to the national economy and the people's livelihood. All merchants and citizens should have a deep understanding of whether the tax rates are appropriate and whether the collection is fair before implementation can proceed smoothly. Now that the regulations for the aforementioned taxes and the collection methods are about to be drafted, our Chamber, being located in Shanghai, the center of national commerce, is closely related to this matter. We hereby send this telegram, hoping that after the tax regulations and collection methods are drafted and implemented, a copy will be provided to us for reference. We would be most grateful. Signed, Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

Telegraphic Request for a Percentage to Protect the Cigarette Industry: Yesterday, the Chamber telegraphed the Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, and the Ministries of Finance and Industry, requesting that a percentage be set aside for protection when collecting the unified cigarette tax. The telegram stated: "According to a letter from the Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Factory Association, 'Upon examining Article 1, Item 4 of the outline for abolishing domestic transit taxes and reforming the special consumption tax, it states that for items that must be encouraged or protected, the government, together with representatives from commercial organizations, will separately formulate measures for encouragement or protection.' This demonstrates the government's intention to respect commercial sentiments and implement protection, for which we are deeply grateful. The suffering of Chinese merchants in the cigarette industry is significantly different from that of other industries. Observers say that due to soaring gold prices and increased tax rates, costs have increased, business has become increasingly difficult, and sales have declined. We are unaware of other industries sharing these conditions. However, the economic invasion by foreign merchants is a fatal blow unique to Chinese merchants. Their capital is abundant, and their organization is complete. Chinese merchants' machines are not as sophisticated, and their experience is not as rich. Moreover, they set up factories in the interior, reducing transportation costs and facilitating supply. Large quantities of raw materials are imported, reducing costs. Investigators are stationed in various ports, and they offer longer credit periods to distribution points, which Chinese merchants with their limited capital cannot imitate. In addition, they have a deep foundation and have been profiting for a long time. If they see an increase in the sales of Chinese cigarettes, they will lower the price of their equivalent cigarettes to compete, and they will purchase and hoard the necessary raw materials for Chinese merchants in large quantities. The expense is only a drop in the bucket from the surplus of the foreign merchants, but it is more than enough to suffocate Chinese merchants. If we do not seek relief, Chinese merchants will have no foothold. Today, our government focuses on the people's livelihood and takes it as its duty to alleviate the suffering of the masses. The abolition of the Likin tax was intended to relieve the people's distress, and the increase in customs duties was intended to protect domestic products. Good policies are issued frequently, and benevolence is spread widely. Chinese merchants are as if they are in the depths of hell, seeing a glimmer of dawn. In the past, speaking out was ineffective, so we chose to remain silent. If we still do not speak out today, we would be burdening the government's good intentions towards protecting merchants and citizens. Examining the practices of European and American countries, when commercial competition occurs, the state allocates funds for subsidies, which is a constant practice. Currently, the entire Chinese cigarette industry is being invaded by foreign goods and has no way to resist. Advancing brings no profit, and retreating is impossible. If we do not formulate separate encouragement and protection measures, the dozens of Chinese cigarette factories and the hundreds of thousands of workers employed by them will feel as if they are drifting in the wind and rain. For the sake of promoting national products and rescuing the people's livelihood, we can only request the government to provide practical protection and approve the allocation of a certain amount from the collection of the unified tax to be used as bonuses. This would give our Chinese cigarette industry a chance to turn around, and the people's livelihood problem could also be partially resolved. The prosperity of the country depends first on the will of the people, and benefiting the country and benefiting the people can be achieved in one fell swoop. We have always admired your Chamber's leadership of merchants and your concern for the people's suffering. Please forward this to the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry to plead for the Chinese cigarette factories and seek a solution.' Based on this, we have investigated that the Chinese cigarette industry has long been affected by the competition from foreign merchants and is limited by its short capital, and is facing dire straits. Therefore, we operate miserably, on the one hand to maintain the survival of national products, and on the other hand to consider the livelihood of hundreds of thousands of workers. Now that the outline of the special consumption tax has been promulgated, regarding the encouragement and protection measures in Article 1, Item 4, the intention to protect domestic products is implied in the average tax burden. If we can be allowed to allocate bonuses from the unified tax collection, not only will the business of Chinese merchants be slightly revived, but it will also show the government's benevolence in implementing protection. Based on the aforementioned situation, it is reasonable to telegraph and earnestly request your ministry to review and implement this, as it would be a great benefit. Signed, Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

The Zhejiang Provincial Government Adopts Shao Dian's Proposal: The Chamber previously telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance, suggesting that it pay attention to the business tax rate when drafting the business tax bill, and that it should follow the central government's regulations that the rate should not exceed two per thousand based on business volume and twenty per thousand based on capital. Yesterday, the Zhejiang Provincial Government replied via telegram, stating, "Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, We have received your Shao Dian telegram. We highly agree with the proposed measures. Before drafting the regulations and implementation rules for the collection of business tax in Zhejiang Province, the Department of Finance first invited leaders from the business community to attend a meeting for public discussion. A preparatory meeting was held on the 17th, and a general meeting was held on the 19th to continue the discussion. As a result, the commercial sentiment was highly agreeable. Signed, Zhejiang Provincial Government, Seal."

Silk Merchants Request a Reduction in Business Tax 102

Sending Representatives to Beijing and Zhejiang to Petition

Since the silk industry in this city heard that the Zhejiang Provincial Government had set the silk business tax at fifteen per thousand of the business tax amount, they believed that the tax levy was too high and they were unable to bear it, causing great anxiety. The Silk Industry Association convened an emergency meeting yesterday, and it was resolved to telegraph the Legislative Yuan and the Ministry of Finance, requesting that the tax be reduced to two per thousand, and to send representatives Wang Yansong, Luo Qinghua, Lu Zhengbing, Pan Xiangsheng, Wu Xingcha, Jiang Linshu, Lou Fengshao, Shen Zicha, and others to the responsible authorities in Beijing and Zhejiang today to petition. The telegram sent by the association to the Ministry of Finance and the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance is recorded as follows:

"Submitting a request that the silk fabric business tax rate in Zhejiang Province is set too high, and merchants are unable to bear it. Please grant the same treatment as the cotton fabric business tax rate, reducing it to two per thousand to maintain sericulture. We respectfully request your review and implementation. It is reported that the regulations for collecting business tax in Zhejiang Province have now been set. Upon examining Article 5, it states that the detailed tax rates for the sale of goods are as specified in the attached table, and upon examining the attached table, it states that the business of selling goods is taxed according to business volume as follows: silk fabric industry, fifteen per thousand. Although the members of the association all have establishments in Shanghai, the majority of the goods they sell are silk fabrics from Zhejiang Province, and some have branches in Zhejiang. According to Articles 7 and 9 of the regulations, they have a direct interest in this matter. After repeated study, we believe that this tax rate is too high and detrimental to the survival of our business. We respectfully present the reasons to your Ministry in detail. Upon examining Article 8 of the Supplementary Measures for the Collection of Business Tax, it states that for those whose taxable base is the amount of business revenue, Article 4 of the Outline shall be followed. Article 4 of the Outline stipulates that the business tax rate shall be calculated using the per thousand method based on the taxable base, and the collection shall not exceed two per thousand, but this does not apply to luxury businesses and other businesses that should be suppressed. The current silk fabric business tax rate set by Zhejiang Province has already exceeded the maximum limit. Presumably, the intention is that silk fabric is considered a luxury business, so the tax rate is particularly high. The first question in this case should be to clarify whether silk fabric is a luxury business. Our country has always been known for establishing itself on agriculture and sericulture, and this has been the case for four thousand years. Since sericulture is the foundation of the nation, and is mentioned together with farming, it is evident that it has never been considered a luxury item. Therefore, the four characters of cloth, silk, beans, and millet have become a common collocation of nouns, which has been passed down to this day, and the clothing of rough cloth and the hat of fine silk have been praised in history as a testament to the frugal virtues of the new nation. Because domestic silk fabrics are strong and easy to wear, although the price is higher than cotton fabrics, the utility is more durable than cotton fabrics. Therefore, purchasing a silk garment that is more durable than a cotton garment may be more economical when calculated in total. According to historical concepts, as such, and based on the facts, we do not want to recklessly regard silk fabrics as luxury items. Furthermore, based on national policy, this time in the customs tariff, apart from tobacco and alcohol, the tax on foreign silk fabrics is the highest. The reason is that our country's silk industry has declined greatly in recent years, and this is intended to maintain it. If it is considered a luxury item, then the country should suppress it, not maintain it. If it is recognized that it should be maintained, it can be proved that it is not a luxury item. Moreover, Japan in Korea and France in Vietnam both consider imported Chinese silk as a luxury item and levy heavy taxes. Our country has also made great efforts to negotiate. Now, for domestic silk fabrics, it is considered to be in the category of luxury items. In the future, if there are similar negotiations, what wording should be used? This is especially a matter that should be considered carefully. Silk fabric is taxed at two per thousand as a manufacturing business tax when it is woven by weaving households, according to Article 4 of the Zhejiang Provincial Business Tax Regulations. When it is sold wholesale, it is also taxed according to Article 7 of the regulations. When it is sold from wholesale to retail stores, it is taxed according to the tax rate specified in the attached table. Moreover, Article 2 of the Special Consumption Tax Regulations clearly stipulates that fabric tax is one of the consumption taxes. Silk fabrics are taxed four times in accordance with current tax law, and the burden is already duplicated. If the set tax rate is too high, stores will be unable to compensate. The only option is to close down. Moreover, the Special Consumption Tax Regulations also distinguish between luxury goods, semi-luxury goods, and daily necessities in terms of the taxable base. If Zhejiang Province classifies silk fabric as a luxury item for business tax, how can silk fabric be unique when the fabric tax is implemented in the future? It will inevitably be oppressed by the double luxury tax, and the silk fabric industry will be even more difficult to survive. After careful consideration, we are really shivering. Recently, many silk factories in Shanghai and Wuxi have been closed down, which is related to the national livelihood. The government has specially approved the issuance of 8 million yuan in public bonds to maintain business needs. Zhejiang Province knows best about the number of silk factories that have closed down and the number of weaving households that have lost their jobs in various parts of Zhejiang Province. The difficult situation is no less than that of silk factories. However, since the issuance of public bonds is an original creation, we dare not ask for an example, and are preparing to ask for tax exemptions to ease the burden. Unexpectedly, this time, when the business tax was created, it was listed in the scope of luxury goods, so that the burden exceeded the maximum limit by seven times as high a tax. Even if all efforts are made, it will be difficult to bear. We dare to present this to your Ministry for review and approval based on the above-mentioned reasons, and respectfully request that you change the example of cotton fabrics and pay tax at two per thousand of the business volume, which is fair. In addition to presenting it to the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance and the Ministry of Finance, we respectfully present it to the Ministry of Finance and the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance."

Yu Youren's Talk 103

Taking Office at the End of This Month

The Control Yuan Will Be Established Next Month

Seeking a Broad Selection of Control Committee Members

Yu Youren, President of the National Government Control Yuan, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing on the morning of the 23rd. Yesterday, he received visitors from various parties at his residence. A reporter from this newspaper made a special visit yesterday to inquire about matters concerning the Control Yuan. I met with Mr. Guofu yesterday (the 23rd), and his illness has improved compared to before. We did not talk about when he will go to Beijing," and so on.

The Case of Japanese Police Officers Insulting Our National Flag in Korea 104

Causing Public Outrage Among Overseas Chinese Merchants

The Japanese Side Has No Response at Present

Regarding the incident of Japanese officials in Korea insulting our national flag, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has lodged a serious protest. Yesterday, according to a friend in diplomatic circles, he received a letter from Zhang Weicheng, the Korean Consul General, which described the incident in detail. It stated: "A few days ago, Chinese businesses in the Hageyu area of ​​Korea, Chunji, Jianchang, Yonghe and other businesses, were notified by the Chinese Consul in Wonsan that they would be closed for five days during the New Year and would hang the national flag to celebrate. They followed this, but on the afternoon of New Year's Day, the chief of the Japanese police station in the area toured the streets and pulled down the Chinese national flags of the businesses and threw them to the ground, showing great anger. Overseas Chinese merchants from Hamhung and other places were greatly outraged by this, and asked the Wonsan Consul to negotiate seriously and put forward conditions: (1) Punish the police chief, (2) The local governor should formally apologize to our consulate. Wonsan Consul Yang negotiated with the local governor but there was no result, so he urgently reported to Zhang Weicheng for instructions on how to deal with the matter. He immediately lodged a serious protest with the Governor-General of Korea, with the aim of punishing and apologizing for the offense. Chinese groups in various parts of Korea have also telegraphed the central government, and the Japanese side has not yet responded," and so on.

Establishment of the Amnesty Committee of the Garrison Headquarters 105

The Amnesty Committee of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters held its inaugural meeting on January 23, 20th year. The attendees were Dai Yuanchuan, Zhong Huan, Liu Tongyi, Zhou Shida, and Su Fuchou. Zhou Shida presided over the meeting, and ceremonial procedures were followed. Dai Yuanchuan gave a report and explained the amnesty regulations. Matters discussed: (1) Discussing the routine notification of various agencies. Resolution: Report to the Ministry of Military Affairs and send letters to various agencies immediately, and order the Second Jiangsu Prison to fill out and submit the names of political prisoners for verification. (2) Discussion on clearing case files. Resolution: The Military Law Department shall first list the names of counter-revolutionary political prisoners sentenced before December 31 of the 19th year and review the files. (3) Discuss the date of the meeting. Resolution: The committee will meet once every Thursday from 1:00 PM to 4:00 PM. (4) Discuss the location of the meeting. Resolution: The first reception room of this headquarters.

The New Ming Ship Has Returned to Shanghai Yesterday 111

Crew Members Describe the Situation When They Were Robbed

The New Ming Ship of the China Merchants Bureau, which was robbed by bandits in Honghai Bay, arrived in Shanghai from Min the previous night at 8 p.m. and berthed at the Jinliyuan Wharf. According to the crew members, the robbery took place at 11:00 p.m. on the 10th of the month, at Xiaobanmen, the sea area bordering Wenzhou and Ningbo. There were a total of eleven pirates hiding in the cabin, averaging about 30 years old. The leader was about 40 years old. They were all dressed in ragged clothes and had simple luggage. When the incident occurred, the man who was about 40 years old gave the order, and each took out a pistol. The crew members were confined in the kitchen, and the passengers were forced into the lower cabin. Each had a thief guarding the door. The engine room, the control room, and the radio station were also occupied. At the same time, the lights were turned off and the robbers began to plunder. The pirates first asked the crew members for the compradors. The Zhang substitute comprador, the Peng second comprador, and the Chen third comprador had all mixed into the passengers. However, the pirates were in a hurry to ask the crew members, so they were about to shoot the Zhang Zhonglian substitute comprador. Zhang Zhonglian had no choice but to come forward. The thieves forced him to hand over the key to the accounting room and the insurance cabin, and the thieves looted them. They also ordered the painters on the ship to paint the yellow chimneys and ship rails of the Xinming ship black. Because the Xiaobanmen area was flanked by two mountains and it was very dark, the thieves were able to wash the ship for two full days and nights. On the morning of the 11th, a pirate ship came to move the stolen goods. A total of ten large boxes of goods were moved away, including eight boxes of Zhi Ni, cigarettes and two boxes of cash. The loss of cash was about 20,000 yuan. There were seven pistols and quick guns on the ship, which were also robbed. The substitute comprador Zhang Zhonglian and four passengers were abducted. One of them has now been rescued in Guangdong.

The Purchasing Agent of Anqing Steamer Arrests the Head of the Tea Room 112

Causing a Serious Labor Dispute

Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 p.m., Fan Chenghua, the purchasing agent of the Taikoo Company's Yangtze River steamer Anqing, sent Zhu Shaobai, the head of the tea room, to the French Concession patrol for punishment, which aroused the opposition of the tea rooms of the entire ship and caused assistance from the tea rooms of other company ships, almost becoming a work slowdown. It has not been resolved yet. The detailed details of the incident are checked and recorded as follows:

Fan Chenghua, who was responsible for collecting subsidies, took over the Anqing wheel last winter. After taking office, he ordered all the tea rooms on the ship to pay two yuan for each meal, that is, six yuan per month, and a total of twenty-seven yuan for each meal in the cabin, and forty-five yuan for each meal in the economy class. Yesterday, when the ship arrived in Shanghai, he asked the head of the tea room, Zhu Shaobai, to collect it. Wang refused to pay because there was no such precedent. Fan then issued an order to dismiss Wang. At 4:30 p.m., Wang was twisted and sent to detention in the French Concession patrol room and ordered to hand it over.

The labor union asked for help. All eighty-nine tea rooms on the ship went to the Seafarers' Union after Wang was arrested to ask for help. The labor union first asked Fan, and Fan replied in a letter, saying that Zhu Shaobai, the head of the ship's room, had failed to pay for meals twice, and had no deposit counter, and was extremely contemptuous, so he had been expelled. The labor union immediately replied in a letter, saying, "We have received a letter stating that the head of the room failed to pay for meals twice and had no formal guarantee, so he has been expelled. While checking, we learned from all the workers on the ship that Zhu Shaobai has been arrested by your director." Matters such as workers failing to pay for meals and having no guarantee can be formally resolved by this union. It is inappropriate for your director to arrest him. You should hand Zhu Shaobai over to the union for management. The ship is about to sail soon. This case cannot be resolved for a while. The current situation will be maintained temporarily and the case will be discussed at a general meeting when Anqing arrives in Shanghai next time (February 4). Deal with Fan severely. All the representatives withdrew."

After this news spread, the tea rooms of various Yangtze River ships in Shanghai, such as Taikoo, China Merchants, Jardine Matheson, and Nissin, learned that Fan Chenghua was oppressing the workers and causing public outrage. Twenty-six representatives were elected from various ships and rushed to the labor union to ask for help. The labor union sent Standing Committee member He Zhenhuan to the ship to negotiate with Fan. He returned to the union at 6:00 p.m. and learned that Zhu had been sent to the French patrol, but Fan refused to hand him over, and there was no result. According to the proposal of the representatives, a final confrontation was planned. After persuasion from the members, the current situation was temporarily maintained. It was decided to wait for Anqing to arrive in Shanghai after work (February 4) to hold a general meeting to discuss the case and deal with Fan severely. The representatives left one after another.

To be Distributed by the Shanghai Office of the Central Relief Committee

Social Affairs Bureau Punishes Rice Boats Adulterating Rice with Water 115

The Ju Xiquan Rice Boat Detained for One and a Half Months

Rice arriving in Shanghai via river often involves the adulteration of rice with water. The Social Affairs Bureau deeply believes that this kind of malicious practice undermines commercial ethics and harms public health. It has repeatedly issued announcements strictly prohibiting such acts. Once verified, the original boat will be confiscated, and the boatmen will be severely punished as a warning. As previously reported, the bureau, based on a report from the Rice Merchants Association, found that a rice boat belonging to Ju Xiquan at the Nanshi rice industry pier was adulterating rice with water. It immediately sent personnel to investigate and, in conjunction with the Public Security Bureau's water patrol, detained the boat and summoned all relevant individuals to the bureau for questioning. After verifying that the rice had indeed been adulterated with water, the boat was confiscated. However, the Nanshi Rice Merchants Association repeatedly pleaded on behalf of the boatman, claiming that he was ignorant and that his entire family depended on the boat for survival. As the prohibition was newly implemented, they may not have been fully aware of it. They requested the bureau to be lenient and pardon this one time. Therefore, the adulterated rice boat was detained at the rice industry pier for one and a half months as a warning. Boatman Ju Xiquan was handed over to the Public Security Bureau for legal punishment, and he was released on bail. The bureau has now announced to all boatmen that any further violations will result in the confiscation of the offending boat without any leniency.

Educational Fees No Longer Collected for Trademark Registration 116

Effective from February 1st

The National Federation of Commerce received instructions from the Ministry of Industry yesterday, stating: To ensure proper implementation, it has been found that since the establishment of the National Registration Bureau, all company and business trademark registrations have been subject to an additional 30% educational fee on top of the registration fee. When the National Registration Bureau was abolished and the Trademark Bureau was established, specializing in trademark registration, and company and business registrations were brought under the Ministry's jurisdiction, the above registrations continued to be processed according to the previous regulations. Now that the Ministry has been organized and its organizational law has been promulgated, matters concerning the registration of companies, businesses, and trademarks will remain under the Ministry's jurisdiction. Effective from February 1st of this year, all the above registrations will be exempt from the additional educational fee to reduce the burden on merchants and the public. This instruction is hereby issued for compliance and dissemination, in addition to separate notifications, for all to follow.

Anhui Merchants in Shanghai Oppose the Rice Permit Fee in Anhui 117

A Disguised Fee After the Abolition of the Likin Tax

The Anhui Rice Merchants Association in Shanghai, regarding the disguised likin fee of two and a half li established in Anhui after the implementation of likin abolition, held an emergency meeting at 2 PM on the 23rd of this month. Standing committee members Yan Tianshan, Jiang Shaoqing, executive committee members Chen Xilin, Wang Yuelou, and over twenty other members attended. Jiang Shaoqing was elected chairman and declared that Anhui has historically been a rice-producing region, and Jiangsu Province has long relied on its supply without any restrictions. The Anhui government's pretext of "imposing a ban through taxation" is causing hardship to the people and harm to businesses more than anything else. After discussion, it was decided to submit a request to the central government for strict prohibition and to record the petition below: "Petition for the strict prohibition of illegal fee collection that harms the people and businesses. We respectfully request a strict order for its abolition." We believe that the government's implementation of likin abolition and tax increases is intended to eliminate the accumulated malpractices of customs barriers, increasing tax revenue for the party and the nation above and easing the burden on the people below. The benevolence of this policy is spreading, and joy is resounding far and wide. However, after the abolition of likin, the Anhui provincial government, citing the pretext of unrestricted rice exports from Anhui, established a Rice Fee Inspection General Office in Wuhu, the capital, and Dasheng Pass, collecting fees of six jiao per dan (unit of dry measure), etc. Since the success of the Northern Expedition, the unification of North and South, and the beginning of political tutelage, everything seeks unification and standardization. In years of abundant harvest in Anhui, exporting rice to supply the people of neighboring provinces, all under the jurisdiction of the National Government, should not be restricted, unlike the re-exporting overseas. Moreover, the National Government has explicitly ordered the abolition of likin, and all similar likin taxes should be abolished. Your province has already implemented this order, but the two-and-a-half li rice fee bureau, similar to likin, still exists in our Anhui. It has changed its name to the Rice Permit Fee Bureau, cleverly establishing new names, arbitrarily increasing fees, and intensifying oppression by sending troops to prevent resistance. Moreover, when collecting fees, the receipts only show twenty or thirty yuan for amounts of one hundred yuan, harming merchants and benefiting those who pocket the difference. Any slight questioning is met with obstruction. Rice merchants' boats are moored on the riverbanks, facing considerable risks, and they dare not argue, enduring the pain and swallowing their anger. Recalling the time before the abolition of likin, each dan of rice, from Anhui to Ningbo, was subject to several customs taxes, totaling only about six jiao. Now, the bureau's fee for each dan of rice is as high as eight or nine jiao. Such arbitrary actions cause hardship to merchants and harm the people. For the sake of maintaining the people's food supply and for the sake of their own businesses, the merchants cannot remain silent and must appeal to your honorable court to promptly and strictly prohibit and fundamentally abolish this fee to uphold the government's decrees and preserve the merchants' livelihood. Respectfully submitted by the Anhui Rice Merchants Association in Shanghai.

Continued Report on the Reception of the British Economic Mission 121

Supplement to the Speeches by Chen Shaokuan and Pan Di

As the British Far East Economic Mission was about to depart, it hosted a reception for various sectors at the Cathay Hotel the night before last to express its gratitude. Deputy Minister of Industry Mu Ouchu, Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council McNeill, and Yu Qiaqing, among others, attended. The farewell address by the head of the delegation, Thomson, was reported in yesterday's newspaper. The responses of Chen Shaokuan, Deputy Minister of the Navy, and Pan Di, British Attorney, are supplemented below:

Chen Shaokuan first thanked the delegation for their warm reception and stated that he, as a naval officer, was not eloquent and could only express his humble opinions in broken English. China is currently in a period of construction, and there is considerable room for the development of British trade with China. He knows that the delegation's visit to China has been very successful and hopes that the delegation members will see what they want to see. In his private opinion, British commerce is indispensable to China, and the delegation's visit is important and timely. He takes the host's cup of wine to wish the delegation members good health and hopes that they will convey to their countrymen the hope that Sino-British trade will see rapid progress on the basis of mutual benefit and that the friendship between the Chinese and British people will also increase.

Pan Di first wished Sir Thomson and the Economic Mission good health and stated that, based on his nine years of experience, he has been to many places, but Shanghai's hospitality is unparalleled. The business community of Shanghai should be grateful to the delegation for leaving their homes and traveling thousands of miles to promote trade with China. Progress of this kind benefits both countries. Furthermore, sticking to one's home and picking up scraps from others is of no practical use, so direct knowledge is the most important. As a lawyer, he often distrusts hearsay evidence because it is not admitted in British courts. He often wonders what a newspaper would be like if a judge were its editor-in-chief. If a judge were to sit in the editor-in-chief's chair, reporters would return to the office with detailed reports of fires, railway accidents, plane crashes, and tragedies. The judge-editor would ask, "Were you at the scene of the fire, railway accident, plane crash, or tragedy?" The reporter would reply, "No, but we have spoken with eyewitnesses." The judge would surely say, "Go away, that is not evidence." The next morning's newspaper would be terrible. Therefore, the best information must be sought from its source. He does not mean that you should not listen to personal opinions, but personal opinions are based on facts. He asks you to examine for yourselves whether the facts are true. Your examination of China will be broad, and you will see the excellent aspects of China. The reports and evidence you collect on trade with China will benefit all parties in the future. We are deeply gratified and look forward to your report.

Renamed National Business Transportation Conference

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce received a respectful telegram from the Ministry of Railways yesterday stating: Having examined the Ministry's calling of the National Railway Freight Rate Conference, as noted in previous telegrams to your Federation, it has been found that many proposals have been put forward, and matters related to business transportation are not entirely within the scope of freight rates. Special News from the Shipping Industry 123

Resolution of the Japanese Warship Collision Case The Yangtze River steamer Hong Yuan of the Sanbei Company collided with the Japanese warship Atago in Hankou last time. The Japanese warship suffered only minor damage. Afterwards, the Japanese side made a request for repair costs. After repeated negotiations with the Sanbei Company, a resolution was reached yesterday. Sanbei acknowledged and paid 600 yuan in repair costs, bringing the matter to a close.

Longshan Towed and Unloaded Cargo The Longshan steamer, which was transporting salt from Haizhou to Hankou, ran aground at Xiaogushan due to shallow water and has been stranded for half a month. The Sanbei Company has now dispatched the Taishan steamer to the scene to quickly unload the salt from the Longshan to lighten the ship's hull. A tugboat will then be dispatched to rescue it.

The Wuneiguan Customs Post Will Not Be Abolished After the implementation of the abolishment of Likin and increased taxation, cotton transported from Longshan in the interior of Ningbo to Yongbo for transshipment by steamer is still being taxed by Yongbo. Various merchant guilds in Shanghai have telegraphed the Ministry of Finance for instructions. Yesterday, they received a reply telegram stating that the abolition of Likin applies to regular customs posts outside of fifty li, while regular customs posts within fifty li will continue to collect taxes. Cotton transported from Longshan to Yongbo is subject to the Wuneiguan tariff and should be taxed according to regulations. The request for exemption should be denied.

Wuxue to Reinstall Water Cables Yesterday, the Ministry of Transportation issued an instruction stating that the aerial cables installed in the Wuxue area have been damaged and cannot be reused. It has been decided to reinstall water cables in the Wuxue section to facilitate telegraph transmission. The materials department has selected two coils of water cable, which will be shipped from Shanghai for reconstruction as soon as possible. The procedure for contracting transportation was already being discussed yesterday.

Shanghai Shipping Merchants Lease Nanshi Waterfront 124

Correspondence Regarding this Matter

Shanghai shipping companies have repeatedly gathered with the Public Utilities Bureau to discuss the lease of the Nanshi waterfront. An agreement has been reached. The correspondence between the Municipal Government and the Shipping Association regarding this case is recorded below.

The Municipal Government to the Shipping Association: With regard to the letter from your association submitted by the Mayor regarding the contract for the lease of the Nanshi waterfront by the shipping companies and the berthing fee, the matter has been discussed and recorded by the Municipal Council. The following amended measures have been determined by our office and the Director of the Land and Public Utilities Bureau after convening representatives of various companies: (1) The rental price will be standardized based on the average of the original price set by the Land Bureau and the price assessed by the Real Estate Evaluation Committee. (2) Article 7 of the Berthing Fee Regulations regarding restrictions on vessels and berthing fees will be temporarily amended as follows for this year: (1) There will be no limit on the number of own vessels; (2) When vessels of other companies berth alongside, two-thirds of the berthing fee will go to the original leasing company and one-third to the Municipal Government. At the end of this year, the situation will be reassessed and re-discussed. In addition to the separate orders issued by the government to the Land Bureau and the Public Utilities Bureau to comply, a corresponding letter is sent to you for your information. Addressed to the Shanghai Shipping Association, Concurrent Acting Secretary-General Yu Hongjun.

Shipping Association to the Municipal Government: In reply, upon receiving your office's Public Letter No. 1083, we have forwarded it to the merchants leasing the wharves and warehouses on the Nanshi waterfront for their information. Afterwards, they claimed that Mr. Yu Qiaqing and Secretary-General Yu had a second face-to-face discussion on this case, and the association sent a letter informing them of the results. They then gathered and discussed the matter themselves. There are still points that need to be corrected and requested, which they are about to present to the Association for submission. Now, we have received the Municipal Government Secretariat's Public Letter, which shows the Municipal Government's concern for the difficulties of merchants and its intention to maintain the shipping industry, for which we are deeply grateful. However, the points that need to be corrected and requested must continue to be presented in order to facilitate matters: (1) The average of the original price set by the Land Bureau and the revised rental price set by the Real Estate Evaluation Committee as the rental price for public land can be reluctantly accepted. Upon receiving notification from the Land Bureau, we will enter into a contract. (2) Article 7, Paragraph 1 of the Berthing Fee Regulations, there is no limit on the number of own vessels. We have received the order, but there are two points that need to be corrected: (A) As a result of the second discussion between Mr. Yu Qiaqing and Secretary-General Yu, there is also no restriction on the number of agency vessels. The facts and reasons why agency and borrowing are different have been detailed in the Municipal Government's summaries and previous discussions. However, the Municipal Government Secretariat's Public Letter does not include the fact that there is no restriction on agency vessels. This is the first point that needs to be corrected. (B) According to the results of the second discussion, the method of allocating the berthing fee for borrowed vessels in three shares is on a trial basis for one year, while there is no agreement for a trial period of one year for the unrestricted number of own vessels. However, the Municipal Government Secretariat's Public Letter also considers the current year as a period of temporary amendment, which is inconsistent with the results of the discussion on that day and is believed to be a miscommunication. This is the second point that needs to be corrected. (3) When other vessels (referring to those that are not agencies but are only borrowing) berth at the wharves leased by the leasing company, the berthing fee will be allocated in three shares: one for the government and two for the merchant. However, in order to avoid ambiguity in fee collection, the leasing company should be requested to issue invoices for this berthing fee and collect it from other vessels. The company will then pay the official share to the Municipal Bank and record it in the register of the Public Utilities Bureau's Wharf and Warehouse Management Office. (4) In the Municipal Government's plan to organize and renovate the Nanshi waterfront wharves, before the addition and relocation of various floating wharves are realized, there are many ships and few wharves, which are insufficient for berthing. This is well known by the government. Allowing other vessels to berth at the wharves leased by the leasing company is actually for the sake of alleviating the difficulties of the Municipal Government and maintaining the operations of the same industry. Therefore, the Municipal Government should be requested to allow the berthing fee to be collected at the old price of Datong and Dada companies and allocated in shares. (5) Once the addition and relocation of the floating wharves are completed according to the renovation plan, the berthing fee for other vessels from Wharf No. 1 to Wharf No. 9 (i.e., within the leased land of the old Datong company) can be collected according to the Berthing Fee Regulations and still allocated in three shares. However, Wharf No. 13 to No. 17 (i.e., within the leased land of the old Datong company) are far from the bustling city center, and most of the vessels berthing are cargo-laden. The Municipal Government should be requested to allow a 30% discount on the price of the Berthing Fee Regulations, which will still be allocated in three shares. (6) The reason for leasing the wharves is to meet the needs and applicability of berthing vessels. However, each wharf is abnormally silted up. Larger ships, even when empty, have difficulty berthing, and smaller ships cannot set sail when fully loaded, resulting in various sufferings such as wasting time, damaging the bottom of the ship, and missing the schedule. The dredging should be expedited and actively carried out at the same time to meet the needs and facilitate the applicability. Otherwise, if the leasing company temporarily delays the payment of the monthly wharf rent, the situation should be viewed with understanding. We are entrusted to forward this information. We hope that you will convey this to the Mayor as much as possible and instruct its implementation to show consistent completion and that all shipping merchants will be more grateful.

The Shipping Association submits a document to the Municipal Finance Bureau requesting its review and instruction: Regarding the various requests made by the merchants leasing the wharves and warehouses on the Nanshi waterfront, which were submitted for review and instruction, the details are described below: (1) Deposit Interest: Article 2 of the already signed wharf contract states that the deposit will bear annual interest of 5%, paid every six months, and drawn with the interest slip issued by the Finance Bureau. In the land lease contract that has not yet been signed but has already been printed, Article 2 also states that the deposit will bear annual interest of 5%, paid every six months, and drawn with the interest slip issued by the Finance Bureau. The annual interest on the deposit must be drawn with the interest slip issued by the Finance Bureau, which is a fixed case that is not easily changed and should be followed. However, the aforementioned interest slip has not yet been issued by the Finance Bureau to the merchants. We request that you forward this and expedite its issuance. (2) The deposit receipt issued by the Finance Bureau seems too ordinary. As this receipt needs to be kept for a long time, a special format should be established to show solemnity. We request that you forward this and consider changing it. (3) The dates on which various merchants paid the deposit are different. We request that you forward this to the Finance Bureau to calculate the first interest payment uniformly to the end of 1929. Afterwards, the interest can be drawn with the slip at the end of June and December each year without any further discrepancies, in order to standardize and facilitate calculation. We request that you forward and review the above three items. We have reviewed that the merchants' so-called forwarding sections are all reasonable and factual requests. Therefore, we respectfully submit this document, hoping that you will approve its implementation. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau.

Local News Two

Ministry of Industry and Commerce Pays Attention to the Liquidation of the Day and Night Bank 129

Yesterday, a telegram ordered the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau to promptly and carefully handle the liquidation.

Lottery-linked savings schemes that have not been approved will be banned.

The ministry ordered the Social Affairs Bureau to expedite the liquidation.

Yesterday, a telegram was received from Nanjing stating that the Shanghai Day and Night Bank and the Great World Savings Department, whose main business is absorbing small deposits, have many depositors who belong to the lower and middle classes of society. Many of them are ordinary people’s hard-earned money. Now, suddenly stopping business for liquidation will have a huge impact on the financial situation of ordinary people’s society. Yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau was telegraphed to promptly and carefully handle the liquidation. Furthermore, since the bank has not been approved for company registration and is not a limited liability company, it should not be liquidated according to the method for limited liability companies to protect the interests of depositors.

Strictly Ban Lottery-Linked Savings: The bureau was also ordered that any unauthorized operation of savings businesses without prior approval, and the exploitation of social vulnerabilities to absorb small savings from ordinary people with high-interest rates and lottery-linked schemes, must be strictly prohibited. Banks that have not been approved for company registration but use the name of a company without authorization should be strictly ordered to apply for registration; otherwise, a letter should be sent to the court to handle them strictly according to the law.

Creditors' Group of the Amusement Department Established: Tang Shengde, Hu Jianxiao, and more than one hundred other creditors of the Great World Savings Amusement Department established a creditors' group office at No. 22 Beijing Road, in the joint office of Wang Zikang, an accountant, and Ni Gang, a lawyer. A founding meeting was convened the day before yesterday, and the attendance was quite crowded. Hu Jianxiao was publicly elected as chairman and Tang Tianmin as secretary. After observing formalities, Hu Jianxiao reported that the Great World Savings Amusement Department is an affiliated organization of the Great World, and all debts should be borne by the directors of the Great World with unlimited liability. He urged the participants to recognize this point and work hard to negotiate. Subsequently, discussions on various issues began. It was resolved that: (1) the group will be named the Great World Savings Amusement Department Creditors' Group to clarify the boundaries and avoid confusion; (2) for the sake of gathering ideas and broadening benefits, a newspaper advertisement will be placed to notify all creditors to register at the office; (3) all expenses will be fully borne by Hu Jianxiao, Tang Shengde, and ten other large creditors to avoid further losses to small creditors; (4) lawyer Ni Gang will be hired as an honorary legal advisor; (5) accountant Wang Zikang will be hired as an honorary accounting advisor to participate in checking the accounts of the amusement department when necessary; (6) other procedures and the selection of staff members will be reported and handled at the first general meeting to be convened on a selected date next week.

Resolutions of the Creditors' Meeting: After the death of the wealthy merchant Huang Chujiu, the Day and Night Bank and the Great World Savings Amusement Department, which he founded, were entrusted to a liquidation committee by the post-mortem committee. However, there is no definite guarantee for the savings. The creditors had no choice but to hold the first meeting of creditors today (January 23) at the law office of Yan Luqing, No. 9 Edward Road. The resolutions are recorded below: (1) This group is named the Day and Night Bank Great World Savings Amusement Department Creditors' Group. (2) This group will temporarily borrow Yan's law office for office space. (3) This group should immediately issue a declaration. (4) If there are creditors who have not joined this group, they should be allowed to continue to register. (5) Please entrust lawyer Yan to guide and handle the affairs of this group. (6) Upon investigation, the depositors' savings are mostly accumulated from meager earnings, and most of them are women and workers. The amounts mostly range from one yuan to several tens or hundreds of yuan, which has a huge impact on the livelihoods of ordinary people. Lawyer Yan has always been known for his righteous and courageous actions, so we specially request lawyer Yan to serve as the honorary lawyer for this case. Lawyer Yan has generously agreed. (7) Send a letter to the Huang Chujiu post-mortem committee, Mr. Yu, Wang, and Yuan, requesting them to put forth effort to handle the matter. (8) Request a balance sheet from the liquidator for the Day and Night Bank Great World Savings Amusement Department as of the date of the business suspension. (9) Investigate all of Huang Chujiu's inheritance. (10) Resolve to make great efforts to achieve the goal of fully recovering the deposits. However, the depositors' savings are accumulated from meager earnings, by scrimping and saving, every penny representing blood and sweat. They are the foundation for the elderly to support themselves, the foundation for the young to start a career, what widows rely on for life, and what children use to study. Once this happens, they are bewildered, disoriented, tears fill their faces, and there is endless pain. Just look at the laborers and shop assistants who have been beating their chests and stamping their feet in front of the two locations for days, and the crying old women and old men. The tragic scene is difficult to describe. At this time of severe winter and cold, the weaker ones may face life-threatening dangers, and the stronger ones may resort to risky actions, creating social unrest. It is heartbreaking to talk about. In terms of legal aspects, lawyer Yan Luqing has generously agreed to serve as an honorary lawyer. We hope that all sectors will show sympathy and provide assistance, which is extremely urgent. January 23, 20th year, at the office of Yan Luqing, lawyer, No. 9 Edward Road.

Twenty-three committee members attended. Chen Jiejie was elected as chairman and Zhu Hailan as secretary. The meeting proceeded as planned. (1) Report: (1) Yesterday, six representatives were elected to go to the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, and various organizations such as the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to present the situation and request assistance. (2) The registration situation today was extremely crowded, with as many as seven or eight hundred people from morning to evening. Among them, workers, women, the elderly, and the weak were the most miserable, mostly with sad faces and tears in their eyes, and even stamping their feet and beating their chests. There were also many students who had deposited all their tuition fees for several years. Once it shakes, it will affect their entire lives, and it is inevitable that there will be words of anger. Countless Diamonds Dazzling, Robbers Took Everything Together 130

Robbery in Kaiming Lane Yesterday Morning

Four Robbers Acted Separately

Diamond Broker Shot

Serious Injuries, Life-Threatening

At around 11:00 AM yesterday, a major robbery occurred at the home of Yong native Qian Meiting, a resident of No. 25, Lane 2, Kaiming Lane, Nine Acres, South City. A large quantity of diamonds worth a great deal of money was robbed, and the owner was shot. The detailed situation is recorded below:

The Family of Ye Yuqian: Ye Yuqian is from Dongting Mountain, Suzhou, 50 years old, and currently works at Zhenkang Foreign Goods Store on Wuxi Road, Public Concession. His home is at No. 24, Lane 2, Kaiming Lane, Nine Acres, South City. However, the single-building stone-gated house next door at No. 25 is also leased by Ye, who acts as a sub-landlord. For convenience, Ye opened another door at the rear staircase entrance, which leads directly to No. 25. The house at No. 25 has four tenants. The ground floor is rented to Qian Meiting, a Yong native engaged in the jewelry business.

Four Robbers Searched and Robbed Separately: At around 11:00 AM yesterday, four robbers suddenly came and entered from the back door of No. 24 under the pretext of asking questions. Three robbers held guns. Two robbers went straight upstairs and into Ye's bedroom, overturning chests and rummaging through everything. The two robbers immediately grabbed Ye's maid, pointed guns to intimidate her into silence, and urgently asked where the Qian family lived, forcing the maid to lead the way. The maid, coerced by the power of the robbers, had no choice but to obey and opened the side door, leading them into No. 25 next door.

Evaluating the Value of Diamonds: Earlier, around 10:00 AM, Zhu Rufa (35 years old), a fellow Ningbo native and jewelry broker who lived at No. 1, Yingfali, Zhangjia Garden, Houjiabang, South City, suddenly came to Qian Meiting's place with a large quantity of diamonds worth a great deal of money to evaluate the price. Qian and Zhu were carefully examining the diamonds in the brighter light in the living room. At this time, in addition to Qian and Zhu, there was also Qian's partner, Xu Xingsheng (24 years old, from Dongting), who was inspecting pearls at another table.

Two Robbers Were Agile: While Qian and Zhu were carefully examining the diamonds, the two robbers suddenly entered the room at the same time, took out their guns, and forbade Qian and the others from making any noise. Qian, seeing this, knew he had encountered robbers and tried to scatter all the diamonds on the table onto the ground in the hope that the robbers would have difficulty picking them up, or that he could take the opportunity to report to the police and get lucky. Unexpectedly, the two robbers had already seen it and rushed forward to grab them all in their hands. At that time, Qian and Zhu were both standing behind the two robbers, intending to muster courage and step forward to capture them. At the opening of the side door, two more robbers rushed in.

Broker Shot While Chasing: When Qian and the others looked back, they saw two more robbers joining them, each holding a gun. They became timid and dared not step forward, but had to wait quietly for instructions. Seeing that the goal had been achieved, the robbers went out through the back door, two running out of No. 24 and two out of No. 25. At that time, the broker Zhu Rufa was anxious and chased after them. Unexpectedly, just as he reached the back door, a robber turned around and fired a shot at him. The bullet entered from the upper part of the left back. But Zhu did not realize it at the time and ran out from the front door to report to the police. When he returned to No. 25, he realized that he had been shot and wounded.

Police Arrived, Robbers Had Fled: When Zhu rushed out to report to the police, the number was very far from the post, and the lane was well connected in all directions. Therefore, when the police arrived, the robbers had already fled far away without a trace. At the same time, Qian, the director of the No. 1 branch of the No. 2 district of Chenxiange, immediately led the police to rush to the scene after hearing the news. But it was too late. They first took Zhu Rufa to Renji Hospital for treatment. After examination by the doctor, it was said that the bullet had hit the lungs but had not penetrated. The situation was quite dangerous.

Details of the Lost Diamonds: This reporter rushed to inquire after hearing the news. According to the sub-landlord Ye Yuqian, when the shooting occurred at No. 25, two robbers were still searching Ye's bedroom at No. 24. They had already taken out a leather robe and a mandarin jacket and were about to put them on to escape when they heard the gunshot downstairs. They abandoned the three pieces of clothing and only robbed forty yuan in small coins, which he said was fortunate. The numbers of the diamonds robbed from Qian's house are recorded below: a total of 485 small diamonds, weighing 31 carats, 13 carats per carat, and more than 40 carats, weighing 5 carats, more than 8 carats per carat, 15 Chinese diamonds, weighing 12 carats, more than 80 points per carat, 15 jade face duck egg rings inlaid with small diamonds, each inlaid with 18 small diamonds, 3 jade chicken hearts and 3 diamond floral arrangements, 4 pairs, 1 dancing ring inlaid with small diamonds, inlaid with 12 small diamonds, a round jade treasure in the middle, plus more than 10 spare parts.

Banditry Outside Songkou 131

Water Police and Bandits in Fierce Battle: Recently, pirates have been rampant outside Wusongkou, appearing and disappearing without a trace, kidnapping and robbing, which happens from time to time. Recently, a fresh pig boat, Jinhetai, carrying more than 170 pigs, docked at Songkou, and the entire cargo was robbed. Although the Fourth District Water Police dispatched police to strictly investigate, there has been no trace. The day before yesterday, each ship escort inspector of the Pig Industry Office in Song was ordered to go to the mouth to investigate. District patrol officer Guan Dianfeng and 17th team patrol officer Gong Shanting supervised and led two escort ships to leave the port. At 11:00 in the evening, on the ocean surface near the fort, they found a fishing boat with suspicious shapes and traces. Just as they were about to approach the boat for inquiry, the bandits in the boat suddenly opened fire. At the same time, three more bandit boats fired fiercely at the two escort boats. Gao and Gong also led the police to return fire. The battle was fierce for more than an hour, and the sound of gunfire was continuous. When the sentry soldiers on the fort heard this, they opened fire remotely from the shore. The bandits began to retreat and fled south. Gao and other patrol officers, due to lack of ammunition and being outnumbered, did not dare to pursue them. They immediately returned to Song and reported to the office, which forwarded the report to the Fourth District Office. At the same time, they joined the 16th team patrol officer Jiang Liang and the 18th team patrol officer Wang Hongzhi, who were stationed in the port with two escort boats, and the 4th platoon of the Water Patrol of the Public Security Bureau, led by squad leader Ding Xiaoping, and patrol officer Song, who led a platoon of water patrol soldiers. They hired a drag and climb dinghy and set off to chase and investigate, reaching tens of miles away, but no trace of the bandit boat was seen. Because it was late at night and dark, it was not easy to pursue deeply. When the escort boats and dinghies returned to Song, it was already dawn. Yesterday, when I went to explore, I saw that there were still twenty or thirty pig boats and many other cargo ships parked outside the mouth, which showed that the bandit boats intended to come and rob the cargo ships. Through this attack, each cargo ship was able to preserve its cargo.

Pirates Engage in Firefight: Pan Kaiwu and Shen Guanxi, two gangs of pirates operating off the coast of Lvsi, outside Wusongkou, had another clash the day before yesterday due to a dispute over fishing donations and maritime boundary issues. Both sides summoned a large number of pirate ships and engaged in a fierce battle on the ocean surface of Daan Port. From 5:00 AM until 3:00 PM, the sound of gunfire had not stopped. Many bandits were killed and injured, and many bandit ships were sunk. It is said that the leader, Pan Kaiwu, had been shot and killed. The Fourth District Water Police has dispatched warships to suppress them. The coastal areas of Tongchonghaiqi counties are afraid that scattered bandits will sneak in, and have dispatched military police to temporarily deploy defenses, which are very strict.

Legal Mother Arranged Marriage With Niece

Biological Mother Did Not Express Consent

Six Thousand Yuan Failed to Settle the Matter

The Wedding Date May Face Problems

Zhang Shiming, a wealthy merchant from Nanxun, is the younger brother of Zhang Jingjiang, a great figure in the Party and the nation. His residence is in Xinchang Lane, Fujian Road. In the past, Zhang was once kidnapped, and then he escaped danger. Zhang was frightened and fell ill, and then passed away. Zhang has a wife, Ms. Xu, and a concubine, Ms. Zhou (namely Zhou Miaoying, 36 years old, from Suzhou), and nine children. His ninth son, named Qu'an, is the son of the concubine Zhou. He is now 18 years old. After Zhang's death, Zhou Miaoying moved to the home of relatives because of disagreement with Xu, while Qu'an still lived in Zhang's house and was raised by Xu. Recently, Zhou learned that Qu'an was going to be married to Xu's niece, but Zhou was not notified. She negotiated with Xu, but it was ineffective. So she hired lawyer Yuan Yang'an to sue in the Special District Local Court, requesting permission for a preliminary injunction, ordering Xu to withdraw this marriage contract, on the grounds that she had not obtained the consent of the biological mother. Later, because there was hope for a settlement, the plaintiff's lawyer requested to withdraw the lawsuit. But after the case was withdrawn, there was no sincerity in the settlement. Zhou also learned that Qu'an had chosen to officially marry at his residence on the 26th of this month (that is, tomorrow), and negotiated with Xu again, but still to no avail. Yesterday, lawyer Yuan published a warning in the newspaper, but it was heard that Qu'an was willing to give his biological mother 60,000 yuan to prevent her from making trouble on the wedding day, while Zhou Miaoying needed 200,000 yuan to settle the matter. This matter has not yet been negotiated. If it cannot be resolved before the 26th, then Zhang Qu'an's wedding date will have to be selected again. The outcome of this case will be continued in the future.

Sued for Failure to Recover

Child Abandoned in an Empty Vat 134

Is There a Complete Egg Under the Overturned Umbrella?

Is It an Illegitimate Child or an Abandoned Child?

Next to the Dasen Cloth Factory at the South End of Sanguantang Town, Pudong,

Page 16

There is a square open space that has been unused for some time, and on the open space are several empty vats belonging to a villager surnamed [blank]. For many days, the day before yesterday, around 6:00 in the morning, a villager surnamed [blank] passed by the place and suddenly saw an umbrella propped up high inside an empty vat. He couldn't help but feel suspicious. There was no room for people inside the empty vat, and although the weather was cloudy, it was not raining. Even if someone were inside, there would be no need to hold an umbrella. He went forward to take a look and found that there was no one under the umbrella, only a rush mat, wrapped quite tightly. The villager did not dare to look at it suddenly at first. He immediately gathered many people to watch and unwrapped the rush mat inside the vat to inspect it. What was stored inside the bag was clearly a newborn baby, only a few days old, with all its clothes. After being touched by people, it suddenly cried loudly. Everyone was greatly surprised, knowing that it was an abandoned child. For a moment, it was passed on by hundreds of people, and they came to watch. Everyone said that this must be an illegitimate child. They were afraid of being discovered, so a few days after birth, they were abandoned by the roadside. Fearing that it would freeze to death, they wrapped it tightly, and fearing that it would rain, they propped it up with two tools to allow families without children to take care of it. At that time, more and more onlookers gathered, and finally a woman surnamed Ling took it away to raise it. The Lu woman had no children at first, and was also bewitched by superstition, saying that raising an illegitimate child could lead to wealth.

Dong Yu Clarifies Dong Jiang's Lawsuit 135

Hiring a Nanny to Educate a Child

Extending Care for Illness

Yesterday's newspaper carried a report about Dong Jiang's divorce case being urged for trial. Dong Yu has sent a letter to clarify the matter. The letter is recorded below:

Respectfully, upon reading the news published in your esteemed newspaper concerning my family affairs, I find it inconsistent with the facts. This case has been ordered by the court for out-of-court settlement. Mediators have been contacted multiple times. Recently, accountant Pan Zhaobang and my uncle Shaoqing earnestly urged me to reluctantly agree to the conditions previously demanded by the other party. Respecting the earnest advice of elders and the good intentions of friends, I reluctantly agreed to accept them all. Unexpectedly, the other party suddenly reversed the previous agreement, creating unnecessary complications, which has delayed the resolution until now. The mediators are all in Shanghai and can easily be consulted for the facts.

The original statement mentions me hiring a teacher for my child's education, which shows a superficial understanding. It should be known that educating children is the parents' inherent duty. Moreover, my son lost his mother in childhood, making him a pitiful motherless child. No one takes care of his diet and clothing in cold weather. As I am tied up with numerous affairs, I cannot spare the time to fully care for him. Therefore, I had to hire a nanny-teacher to provide protection. I entrusted many people to find one, and recently, my friend Mr. Chen Ronglu introduced Ms. Cheng to fill the position. However, the employment contract has not been finalized, as I am still unsure whether my son will obey her teaching. The claim of two female teachers is even more of a misunderstanding.

Recently, my son and I both contracted a cold, causing us great distress. My friend Mr. Qiu Zijia introduced Dr. Wang Yongchuan of the Red Cross to treat us. Knowing that we lacked care during our illness, he entrusted Dr. Wang to invite Mr. and Mrs. Xu Yefu to our residence to provide nursing care. The other party deliberately exaggerates this, and I truly do not understand their intentions.

Driven by responsibility and livelihood, even while bedridden, I cannot isolate myself from everything and concentrate solely on recovery. I still receive concerned parties before my sickbed. As the other party stated, anyone with a shred of conscience should show pity, yet they heartlessly use this as a reason to attack me. What kind of heart is this? It is truly extreme.

The lack of order in my family did not begin today. The day my first wife, Ms. Lu, passed away was the day my family lost its order. Thinking of this, my heart aches immensely. If the other party wants a clear distinction of status as soon as possible, they should quickly come to their senses and understand the court's intention to settle matters peacefully. Accommodating the good intentions of relatives and friends in mediation will surely fulfill their wishes. If they continue to indulge in unrealistic fantasies and offer temporary solutions to superficial problems, it may not be the right path. I have specifically presented the detailed facts to respectfully request a correction to reveal the truth and sincerely express my public obligations.

A Woman Crushed to Death by a Songhu Train in Shanghai 137

Body Smashed into Two Pieces

The Songhu Railway's upward-bound train number 103 departed from Paotaiwan Station at 4:50 PM yesterday. When it reached Wai Yang Qi Tai, the driver glimpsed a woman walking on the iron bridge. The driver immediately sounded the whistle to warn her, but upon hearing the loud whistle, the woman panicked, causing her to fall on the bridge and struggle to get up. Seeing this, the driver immediately closed the valve and stopped the engine. However, due to inertia, the train continued forward, and the wheels ran over the woman's body, killing her instantly.

After the train stopped, the driver and the guard got out to inspect the scene. They observed that the woman was about forty years old, wearing old blue cloth clothes, with small feet. Her entire body was crushed into two pieces by the train wheels. The nearby tracks were stained with fresh blood, a gruesome sight. Subsequently, the train arrived at Wusong Town Station, and the guard reported to the stationmaster, who sent laborers to the scene of the accident to remove the body from the tracks, prepare a coffin for burial, and await identification by relatives. They also reported the matter to the Railway Bureau for investigation.

Chinese Constable Dies from Serious Injuries 138

Automobile Company to Provide Compensation

Chinese Constable No. 3069 of the Public Concession was riding his bicycle on Yangshupu Road the day before yesterday. At that time, automobile No. 5058 was approaching from the opposite direction. The constable's bicycle suddenly moved in front of the car. The driver, Xu A'er, steered to avoid it, but the car's wing struck the constable's nose, causing him to fall. The car also crashed into a tree on the side of the road. People transported the constable to the Public Works Department Hospital for treatment. He was identified as Jin Dexin. Shortly afterward, he died from his injuries. His body was sent to the coroner's office. Yesterday morning, Special Court Commissioner Guo inspected the body and ruled that it be handed over to his brother, Jin Dexiang, for burial. He also instructed the automobile company to provide appropriate compensation.

Lawyer Fails to Appear in Court Three Times After Being Entrusted 139

Client Suffers Great Loss

Forced to File a Complaint

Lawyer Wu Chengyu from Guangdong was previously sued by the Shanghai Bank in the Special District Court for cleaning up the accounts of the Drunken Heaven Restaurant. This has already been reported in the newspapers. Recently, Gao Bingjiang from Zhenhai filed a criminal complaint against Wu in the Special Court for breach of trust and destruction of property. Gao, who resides at No. 34 Mingyuan Lane, Huade Road, was previously the head of a post office branch. Last August, he was sued in court by a woman named Wang Lu for abandonment. Gao hired Lawyer Wu to defend him, agreeing to a fee of 60 yuan, with 30 yuan paid in advance, for which Wu issued a receipt. However, Wu failed to appear in court for the three subsequent hearings, leading to Gao's detention. Gao argues that Wu, having been entrusted and received the fee, failed to appear in court, thereby committing breach of trust and other crimes. Therefore, he filed a criminal lawsuit. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ge Zhitan of the Special Court opened the court for interrogation. The defendant, Wu Chengyu, did not appear, but a lawyer appeared on his behalf, stating that Wu was attending court in the Jiangsu High Court and was therefore unable to attend. He requested a postponement and presented the High Court summons for inspection. Judge Ge then declared to Wu's representative lawyer that breach of trust and other crimes are punishable by imprisonment, therefore Wu himself must be present in court. The hearing was postponed to allow Wu to appear for questioning next time.

Wife of a Ticket Seller Goes Missing 144

Wang Fugen, 32 years old, a local from Shanghai, who works as a ticket seller at the Public Concession Bus Company, resides at No. 42 Xinkang Lane, near Caojiadu on the western outskirts of Shanghai. In August of the 16th year of the Republic, he was introduced by a friend and began cohabitating with Ms. Su, a local woman, who is 28 years old. They were very affectionate and loving. Wang went out to work every day, and Ms. Su diligently managed the household, being very well-behaved. As time passed, Wang, considering her to be very simple and honest and capable of growing old together, took her as his wife. Relatives also treated her with respect and courtesy. Unexpectedly, after more than three years, she suddenly changed her usual behavior. She often went out to play with her female friends, neglecting household affairs. Although Wang repeatedly tried to stop her and took precautions, it was ultimately ineffective. The afternoon before yesterday, while Wang was working on the bus, Ms. Su took all of her clothes, jewelry, and other belongings (worth about 200 yuan) and fled without a trace. Wang returned home and discovered this, searching everywhere but finding nothing. Yesterday, Wang submitted a report with a photo attached to the Sixth District Police Station and the Jing'an Temple Police Station, requesting that they investigate and apprehend his runaway wife.

Establishment of the Modern Arts Society 146

The illusionist master Ji Tianxiang has recently returned from Europe and America. Observing the dullness of the domestic art scene, he has gathered various famous artists to organize a large-scale art group, named the Modern Society. They have rented a magnificent western-style building at No. 6 Lishui Lane, Tamsui Road, Aidao Ya Road, as the society's headquarters. It is divided into three departments: Song and Dance, Drama, and Illusion. The Song and Dance Department is jointly led by Zhao Xianglin, a famous song and dance performer, and Yin Yiqiu, the founder of the Pear Blossom Girls' Song and Dance Troupe and former professor of the China Song and Dance College. Most of the performers are outstanding members of Pear Blossom and Yin's talented students. The Drama Department is led by the veteran dramatist Ling Xinzi. The Illusion Department is jointly led by Ji and Li Mingxing, the Fire King who once caused a sensation at home and abroad. The talent within is abundant, and the future is immeasurable. It is truly good news for art lovers. It is also heard that the Song and Dance Department of the society still needs to recruit dozens of female performers. Whether they have studied before or not, they can register for the examination. The remuneration is said to be very generous.

Sheng Yufu, 47 years old, from Shaoxing, resides in Wusong West City and is engaged in the business of collecting paper ingots and ashes. His face and right arm bones were crushed and bloody, a gruesome sight.
